## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the acceleration equation of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of velocity and time. The nonlinearity likely appears in damping terms (velocity-dependent) and/or restoring forces (encoded through time dependence), consistent with classic nonlinear oscillator models like van der Pol or Duffing oscillators.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear damping: dv_dt = c0 * v (simple viscous damping)
- Harmonic driving: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t + c2) (periodic external force)
- Damped driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (linear damping with periodic drive)
- Van der Pol type: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * v**2) * v (nonlinear damping term)
- Cubic velocity nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 (polynomial nonlinear damping)
- Quadratic-cubic velocity: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**2 + c2 * v**3 (general nonlinear damping)
- Van der Pol driven: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * v**2) * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (nonlinear damping with drive)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v * (1 - c1 * v**2) + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (Rayleigh-type nonlinearity)
- Restoring via trig: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t + c2) + c3 * v (position encoded as phase of oscillation)
- Duffing-like driven: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * sin(c2 * t) + c3 * sin(c2 * t)**3 (cubic restoring force with known frequency)
- Nonlinear damping + drive: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * cos(c3 * t + c4) (general nonlinear oscillator)
- Coulomb + viscous: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * sign(v) + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (mixed friction with drive)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * v**5 (higher-order nonlinear damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Velocity-dependent damping nonlinearity → odd powers of v (v, v**3, v**5) preserve symmetry of oscillation
- Self-sustained oscillation (limit cycle) → terms like (1 - c*v**2)*v indicating amplitude-dependent damping sign change
- Periodic external forcing → sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms representing harmonic driving forces
- Position information absent but system oscillatory → position may be reconstructable as integral of v, or encoded through trigonometric functions of t
- Energy-based nonlinearity → v**2 * v terms represent velocity-dependent energy dissipation/injection
- Frequency mixing in driven systems → products of sin/cos(t) with powers of v indicate parametric coupling
- Phase-space reduction → when dv/dt = f(v) only (no explicit t), the system is autonomous and analyzable via phase portraits
- Even powers of v (v**2) break time-reversal symmetry → indicate asymmetric damping or rectification effects
